Such symptoms are rare after LASIK and are most often associated with dry eyes, which in most people, returns to preoperative levels within a few months after surgery. Additionally, it is common for people to experience difficulties with near vision at some point after age 40. This is called Presbyopia and is a natural change in the eyes' ability to focus.\n\nWhen evaluating a patient for LASIK surgery, it is important that your surgeon look for and treat signs and symptoms of dry eye. < text>
Generally food is O.K.+, very busy at times ("location,location"). However I was EXTREMELY disappointed this time: normally I only eat some of the chips and leave the rest in the basket, except this time at halfway down the basket I started to notice the chips felt moist, then soggy. So, perplexed, I emptied the basket of the remaining chips and to my horror, found the rest of the chips were covered with old beans and salsa and salsa drippings all in the bottom of the basket. I spoke to the owner, who was previously cleaning the restaurant's tables, and asked if they were "recycling people's leftover chips" all the explanation he gave was a "No, if you want to look at the kitchen trash can, you can find some chips"...No sorry, NOTHING! :(....It was a bad, nauseous experience, I won't be going back...I don't think I'll trust another basket if chips ANYWHERE else again without checking to see if they're someone else's "recycled chips"...or salsa bowls, for that matter!</text>
